**97.** Fan blades: 60 cm diameter, rotating at 120 rpm. Speed of tip:

$v = \omega r = (120 \times 2\pi/60) \times 0.3 = 4\pi \times 0.3 = 1.2\pi \approx 3.77$ m/s.

(A) $0.6\pi$ m/s &nbsp;&nbsp; (B) $1.2\pi$ m/s &nbsp;&nbsp; (C) $2.4\pi$ m/s &nbsp;&nbsp; (D) $4.8\pi$ m/s

---

**98.** A particle in non-uniform circular motion: at some instant speed is 6 m/s and increasing at 8 m/s². Radius = 3 m. The angle of net acceleration with centripetal direction:

$a_c = 36/3 = 12$ m/s²; $a_t = 8$ m/s².

$\tan\phi = 8/12 = 2/3 \Rightarrow \phi = \tan^{-1}(2/3) \approx 33.7°$.

(A) $\tan^{-1}(3/2)$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (B) $\tan^{-1}(2/3)$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (C) $45°$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (D) $53°$

---

**99.** A second hand of a clock (length 10 cm). Centripetal acceleration of its tip:

$T = 60$ s; $\omega = 2\pi/60$ rad/s; $a_c = \omega^2 r = (2\pi/60)^2 \times 0.1 = 4\pi^2 \times 0.1/3600 \approx 1.1 \times 10^{-3}$ m/s².

(A) $1.1 \times 10^{-3}$ m/s² &nbsp;&nbsp; (B) $1.1 \times 10^{-2}$ m/s² &nbsp;&nbsp; (C) $\pi^2 \times 10^{-3}$ m/s² &nbsp;&nbsp; (D) $2 \times 10^{-3}$ m/s²

---

**100.** A particle starts from rest and moves with uniform tangential acceleration $\alpha$ on a circular path of radius $R$. The net acceleration after it has turned through angle $\theta$:

$v^2 = 2\alpha R\theta$; $a_c = v^2/R = 2\alpha\theta$; $a_t = \alpha$.

$|a| = \sqrt{(2\alpha\theta)^2 + \alpha^2} = \alpha\sqrt{4\theta^2+1}$.

(A) $\alpha\sqrt{4\theta^2+1}$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (B) $\alpha(2\theta+1)$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (C) $2\alpha\theta$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (D) $\alpha\sqrt{4\theta+1}$

---

**Quick-check solutions for selected problems:**

**Q2:** Harmonic mean of speeds for equal distances: $\bar{v} = \frac{2 \times 40 \times 60}{40+60} = 48$ km/h.

**Q7:** Both start from rest; distances $\propto a$; ratio = $a : 3a = 1:3$.

**Q8:** $v^2 = u^2 - 2as$: $100^2 - 300^2 = -2a(0.1)$; $a = (90000-10000)/0.2 = 400000/2 = 4 \times 10^5$ m/s².

**Q10:** $x_1 = 2a(2) = 4a$; $x_2 = 2a(2+2+2) - x_1$... using $x_2 - x_1 = a t^2 = a \times 4 = 4a$... wait:

$x_1 = ut + \frac{1}{2}at^2 = \frac{1}{2}a(4) = 2a$ (from rest). $x_2$ in next 2s: total after 4s $= \frac{1}{2}a(16) = 8a$; so $x_2 = 8a - 2a = 6a$. $x_2 - x_1 = 4a$. ✓ Answer A.

**Q14:** $s = kt^{3/2} \Rightarrow v = \frac{3k}{2}t^{1/2} \Rightarrow a = \frac{3k}{4}t^{-1/2}$. Now $v = \frac{3k}{2}t^{1/2}$ so $t^{1/2} = 2v/(3k)$, giving $a \propto 1/t^{1/2} \propto 1/\sqrt{s^{1/3} \cdot ...}$. More directly: $v^2 = \frac{9k^2}{4}t$; and $s = kt^{3/2}$ so $t = (s/k)^{2/3}$; then $a = \frac{3k}{4}(s/k)^{-1/3} \propto s^{-1/3}$. Answer A.

**Q15:** $s_n = \frac{a}{2}(2n-1)$ from rest. $d_1 = a/2$; $d_3 = 5a/2$. Ratio $= 1:5$. Answer A.

**Q18:** $S_1 = ut + \frac{1}{2}at^2$; $S_1 + S_2 = 2ut + 2at^2$. So $S_2 = ut + \frac{3}{2}at^2$. $S_2 - S_1 = at^2 \Rightarrow a = (S_2-S_1)/t^2$. Answer A.

**Q19:** A ball is dropped from $H = 80$ m at the same instant another is thrown up from the ground at $40$ m/s. Both share the same $-5t^2$ term, so it cancels when their heights are equated: $80 - 5t^2 = 40t - 5t^2 \Rightarrow 80 = 40t \Rightarrow t = 2$ s. Meeting height: $y = 40(2) - 5(2)^2 = 80 - 20 = 60$ m. Answer D.

**Q20:** $a = 10 - 2t = 0$ at $t = 5$ s. $v(5) = \int_0^5 (10-2t)dt = [10t-t^2]_0^5 = 50-25 = 25$ m/s. Answer C.

**Q21:** $v^2 = 4 + 4s$. Differentiate: $2v\dot{v} = 4\dot{s} = 4v \Rightarrow a = 2$ m/s². Answer B.

**Q22:** Relative speed = $(72+108)/3.6 = 50$ m/s. $t = 1800/50 = 36$ s. Answer C.

**Q23:** At $h = H/2$: $v^2 = u^2 - 2g(H/2) = u^2 - gH = u^2 - u^2 = 0$... No, $H = u^2/2g$, so $gH = u^2/2$. $v^2 = u^2 - u^2/2 = u^2/2 \Rightarrow v = u/\sqrt{2}$. Answer B.

**Q24:** $0 = 60 + 20t - 5t^2 \Rightarrow t^2 - 4t - 12 = 0 \Rightarrow (t-6)(t+2) = 0 \Rightarrow t = 6$ s. Answer C.

**Q25:** $v = \int_0^3 2t\,dt = [t^2]_0^3 = 9$ m/s. Answer B.

**Q27:** $a = -30/6 = -5$ m/s². Distance in last 2s: use $v(4) = 30 - 5(4) = 10$ m/s. In 4→6 s: $s = 10(2) + \frac{1}{2}(-5)(4) = 20 - 10 = 10$ m. Answer A.

**Q30:** $v^2 = u^2 - 2as$; $0 = u^2 - 2as \Rightarrow a = u^2/2s$. At distance $s/4$: $v^2 = u^2 - 2(u^2/2s)(s/4) = u^2 - u^2/4 = 3u^2/4 \Rightarrow v = u\sqrt{3}/2$. Answer A.

**Q36:** Phase 1: $3 \text{ s} \times 12 \text{ m/s} = 36$ m. Phase 2: $3 \text{ s} \times 8 \text{ m/s} = 24$ m. Total distance $= 36 + 24 = 60$ m. Answer C.

**Q46:** $H = u^2\sin^2\theta/(2g) = 400 \times 0.5/(20) = 10$ m. Answer B.

**Q48:** $t = \sqrt{2 \times 45/10} = 3$ s; $R = 10 \times 3 = 30$ m. Answer C.

**Q49:** $T = 2u_y/g \Rightarrow u_y = gT/2$. Answer A.

**Q53:** Answer A: $u = 2\sqrt{5}$ m/s.

**Q56:** $R = 4H$ at $\theta = 45°$: $H = R/4 = 40/4 = 10$ m. Answer C.

**Q59:** At peak: $v = u\cos\theta$; all $g$ is centripetal ($a_n = g$): $\rho = (u\cos\theta)^2/g = u^2\cos^2\theta/g$. Answer A.

**Q63:** Speed at peak $= u\cos\theta$; radius of curvature $= (u\cos\theta)^2/g = u^2\cos^2\theta/g$. Answer B.

**Q65:** Perpendicular: $\vec{v}_0 \cdot \vec{v}(t) = 0$: $(10)(10) + (10)(10-10t) = 0 \Rightarrow 200 - 100t = 0 \Rightarrow t = 2$ s. Answer C.

**Q76:** $D_{min} = 100\sqrt{7}/3$ m. Answer B.

**Q80:** $v_r = 2$ m/s. Answer B.

**Q83:** $\alpha = d\omega/dt = 3$ rad/s² (constant). Answer B.

**Q93:** $2\sqrt{5}$ m/s² = $\sqrt{20}$ m/s² ≈ 4.47 m/s². Answer B.

**Q100:** $|a| = \alpha\sqrt{4\theta^2+1}$. Answer A.

</details>

---


## Part B — JEE Advanced Practice (Problems 1–75)

*Mixed formats: Single correct (SC), Multiple correct (MC), Integer type (IT), Paragraph-based (PB).*

---

### Block 1: 1D Motion — Complex (Adv. 1–15)

**Adv. 1.** *(SC)* A particle starts from rest at $x = 0$ and moves with acceleration $a = 6 - 2x$ m/s² (where $x$ is in m). The particle first comes to rest again at:

(A) $x = 3$ m &nbsp;&nbsp; (B) $x = 6$ m &nbsp;&nbsp; (C) $x = 4$ m &nbsp;&nbsp; (D) $x = 9$ m

---

**Adv. 2.** *(MC)* $x(t) = 2t^3 - 9t^2 + 12t - 4$. Which of the following are correct?

(A) Particle is at rest at $t = 1$ s and $t = 2$ s

(B) Particle moves in $+x$ direction for $t > 2$ s

(C) Particle is at $x = 1$ m at $t = 1$ s

(D) Total distance in $t = 0$ to $t = 3$ s is 2 m

---

**Adv. 3.** *(IT)* A particle has $v^2 = 4(4x - x^2)$. The maximum value of velocity (in m/s) is: **\_\_\_\_**

---

**Adv. 4.** *(SC)* A stone is dropped into a well of depth $H$. The splash is heard after time $T$. If speed of sound is $v_s$ and $g$ is acceleration due to gravity, then $H$ satisfies:

(A) $H = \frac{v_s^2}{g}\left(1 - \sqrt{1 - \frac{gT}{v_s}}\right)^2$

(B) $H = \frac{1}{2}g\left(T - \frac{H}{v_s}\right)^2$

(C) $H = \frac{g}{2}\left(\frac{v_s}{g}\right)^2\left(1-\sqrt{1-\frac{2gT}{v_s}}\right)^2$

(D) Both B and C are equivalent correct expressions

---

**Adv. 5.** *(SC)* Two particles A and B start simultaneously from the same point on a circular track of circumference 120 m. A moves at 6 m/s (clockwise) and B at 10 m/s (anticlockwise). They first meet after time:

(A) 7.5 s &nbsp;&nbsp; (B) 10 s &nbsp;&nbsp; (C) 6 s &nbsp;&nbsp; (D) 12 s

---

**Adv. 6.** *(IT)* A body starts from rest. In the first $n$ seconds it covers distance $S_1$; in the next $n$ seconds distance $S_2$; in the next $n$ seconds $S_3$. Value of $S_1 : S_2 : S_3$: write $S_3/(S_1)$ as an integer. **\_\_\_\_**

---

**Adv. 7.** *(SC)* Particle A: $x_A = 4t + 2t^2$. Particle B starts from rest at $x = 8$ m at $t = 0$ with acceleration 4 m/s². Time when they meet:

(A) 1 s &nbsp;&nbsp; (B) 2 s &nbsp;&nbsp; (C) 3 s &nbsp;&nbsp; (D) They never meet

---

**Adv. 8.** *(MC)* For a particle with $a = f(v)$ (function of velocity only):

(A) $v\,dv/dx = f(v)$ can be used to find $v(x)$

(B) $dv/dt = f(v)$ can be used to find $v(t)$

(C) The motion is always periodic

(D) SUVAT equations apply if $f(v) = $ constant

---

**Adv. 9.** *(SC)* Ball A is dropped from height $2H$ and ball B is dropped from height $H$ at the same instant. When B hits the ground, what is the distance between A and B?

$t_B = \sqrt{2H/g}$. Ball A falls: $h_A = \frac{1}{2}g t_B^2 = H$. Ball A is at height $2H - H = H$ above ground. Ball B is at ground. Separation $= H$.

(A) $H/2$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (B) $H$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (C) $2H-H\sqrt{2}$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (D) $H(\sqrt{2}-1)$

---

**Adv. 10.** *(IT)* A particle decelerates uniformly from 20 m/s and comes to rest in 5 s. The ratio of the distances covered in the 1st and 3rd seconds is $p/q$ in lowest terms. Find $p + q$. **\_\_\_\_**

Deceleration $a = 20/5 = 4$ m/s². Distance in the $n$-th second: $s_n = u - \frac{a}{2}(2n-1)$.

$s_1 = 20 - 2(1) = 18$ m; $s_3 = 20 - 2(5) = 10$ m. Ratio $= 18:10 = 9:5$, so $p + q = 14$.

---

**Adv. 11.** *(SC)* $x = A\cos(\omega t + \phi)$. Which of the following is a correct statement about this motion?

(A) It is uniformly accelerated motion (B) It is SHM with amplitude $A$ (C) Velocity is constant (D) Acceleration is zero

---

**Adv. 12.** *(SC)* A train accelerates uniformly from rest to $v$ m/s in time $T_1$ s, runs at constant $v$ for $T_2$ s, then decelerates uniformly to rest in $T_3$ s. Total distance:

(A) $v(T_1/2 + T_2 + T_3/2)$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (B) $v(T_1 + T_2 + T_3)$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (C) $v(T_2 + T_3)$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (D) $\frac{v}{2}(T_1 + 2T_2 + T_3)$

---

**Adv. 13.** *(MC)* A stone is thrown vertically upward with speed $u$. The ratio of distances covered in the $n$th and $(n+1)$th second of ascent is:

(A) $(2n-1):(2n+1)$ after sign consideration

(B) The ratio approaches 1 as $n \to \infty$

(C) In ascent, $s_n = u - g(2n-1)/2$, decreasing each second

(D) The ball always ascends for exactly $u/g$ seconds

---

**Adv. 14.** *(IT)* A ball is dropped from height $H$. It loses $\frac{1}{4}$ of its kinetic energy each time it bounces. After how many bounces does the bounce height first fall below $H/4$? **\_\_\_\_**

After each bounce, KE is $3/4$ of KE before, so height is $3/4$ of previous. After $n$ bounces: $H(3/4)^n < H/4 \Rightarrow (3/4)^n < 1/4$. $(3/4)^1 = 0.75$, $(3/4)^2 = 0.5625$, $(3/4)^3 \approx 0.422$, $(3/4)^4 \approx 0.316$, $(3/4)^5 \approx 0.237 < 0.25$. Answer: 5.

---

**Adv. 15.** *(SC)* A particle at $x = 0$ has $v = 0$ and $a = 4$ m/s² at $t = 0$. If $a = 4 - 2v$, maximum velocity:

$a = 0$: $4 - 2v = 0 \Rightarrow v_{max} = 2$ m/s.

(A) 1 m/s &nbsp;&nbsp; (B) 2 m/s &nbsp;&nbsp; (C) 4 m/s &nbsp;&nbsp; (D) 8 m/s

---

### Block 2: Projectile Motion — Advanced (Adv. 16–30)

**Adv. 16.** *(SC)* A particle is projected at $u$ and $\theta$. The radius of curvature at the point where velocity makes angle $\phi$ with horizontal is:

(A) $\dfrac{u^2\cos^2\theta}{g\cos^3\phi}$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (B) $\dfrac{u^2}{g\cos^2\phi}$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (C) $\dfrac{u\cos\theta}{g\cos^2\phi}$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (D) $\dfrac{u^2\cos\theta}{g\cos^2\phi}$

---

**Adv. 17.** *(IT)* A projectile is fired at $u = 10\sqrt{2}$ m/s and $\theta = 45°$. The speed when its velocity makes $30°$ with the vertical ($g = 10$ m/s²): **\_\_\_\_** (integer in m/s)

Velocity makes 30° with vertical = 60° with horizontal. At that instant: $v_x = v\cos60° = v/2$. But $v_x = u\cos45° = 10$. So $v = 20$ m/s.

Answer: 20 m/s.

---

**Adv. 18.** *(MC)* For a projectile from ground, which statements are correct?

(A) The trajectory is a parabola in the absence of air resistance

(B) Velocity is perpendicular to acceleration at the highest point only

(C) The time to reach maximum height equals the time to come back (same level)

(D) The horizontal component of velocity is zero at maximum height

---

**Adv. 19.** *(SC)* A gun fires shells at $u = 100$ m/s. A target is at horizontal distance 800 m and height 100 m. The sine of the angle of projection is: ($g = 10$ m/s²)

Trajectory: $y = x\tan\theta - \dfrac{gx^2}{2u^2\cos^2\theta}$. At $(800, 100)$, writing $T = \tan\theta$ and $\frac{1}{\cos^2\theta} = 1 + T^2$:

$$100 = 800T - 320(1 + T^2) \Rightarrow 16T^2 - 40T + 21 = 0 \Rightarrow T = \frac{40 \pm 16}{32} = \frac{7}{4} \text{ or } \frac{3}{4}$$

For $\tan\theta = \frac{3}{4}$: $\sin\theta = \frac{3}{5}$. For $\tan\theta = \frac{7}{4}$: $\sin\theta = \frac{7}{\sqrt{65}}$. Both the low and high trajectories reach the target.

(A) $3/5$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (B) $4/5$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (C) $7/\sqrt{65}$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (D) Both A and C

---

**Adv. 20.** *(IT)* A projectile is fired at $u = 50$ m/s and $\theta = 37°$ ($\sin37° = 0.6$, $\cos37° = 0.8$, $g = 10$ m/s²). When it has traveled a horizontal distance of 120 m, its speed (in m/s) is: **\_\_\_\_**

$u_x = 50\cos37° = 40$ m/s, $u_y = 50\sin37° = 30$ m/s. Time to cover 120 m horizontally: $t = 120/40 = 3$ s. Then $v_y = 30 - 10(3) = 0$ (the ball is at its peak), so the speed is $v_x = 40$ m/s.

Answer: **40**

---

**Adv. 21.** *(SC)* A particle is projected from the ground at angle $\theta$ and speed $u$. It hits a vertical wall at horizontal distance $d$ with vertical velocity $v_y$ downward. Which statement about the wall is correct?

Horizontal: $d = u\cos\theta \cdot t \Rightarrow t = d/(u\cos\theta)$.
Vertical velocity at wall: $v_y = u\sin\theta - gt$. If $v_y < 0$ (downward), the ball has passed its peak.

(A) The wall must be beyond the range

(B) The ball hit the wall on its way down

(C) The ball hit the wall on its way up

(D) The ball hit the wall exactly at the highest point

---

**Adv. 22.** *(MC)* A ball is thrown at angle $\theta$ and just clears a wall of height $h$ at distance $R/2$ (half the range). Correct statements:

(A) $\tan\theta = 4h/R$ (comparing trajectory at $x = R/2$: $h = \frac{R}{2}\tan\theta(1-\frac{1}{2}) = R\tan\theta/4$, so $\tan\theta = 4h/R$) ✓

(B) The ball hits the ground at range $R$

(C) The wall is at the peak of the trajectory

(D) Maximum height $= 2h$

---

**Adv. 23.** *(SC)* A stone is thrown from a cliff of height $H$ at angle $\alpha$ above horizontal with speed $u$. The time to reach the base of the cliff (directly below the launch point) where the stone lands at horizontal distance $d$:

$(t_{base}): d = u\cos\alpha \cdot t_b$; base is at $y = 0$ (ground below cliff): $0 = H + u\sin\alpha \cdot t - \frac{g}{2}t^2$.

(A) $t_b = \frac{u\sin\alpha + \sqrt{u^2\sin^2\alpha + 2gH}}{g}$

(B) $t_b = \frac{u\cos\alpha}{d/t_b}$ (circular)

(C) $d = u\cos\alpha\cdot\frac{u\sin\alpha + \sqrt{u^2\sin^2\alpha + 2gH}}{g}$

(D) Both A and C

---

**Adv. 24.** *(IT)* A ball projected at $u = 10$ m/s from the edge of a table of height $h = 5$ m. How many seconds does it remain in the air if launched at $30°$ below horizontal? ($g = 10$ m/s²) **\_\_\_\_**

$u_x = 10\cos30° = 5\sqrt{3}$; $u_y = -10\sin30° = -5$ m/s (downward).

$0 = 5 - 5t - 5t^2 \Rightarrow t^2 + t - 1 = 0 \Rightarrow t = (-1 + \sqrt{5})/2 \approx 0.618$ s. Not integer.

Use $u = 10$ m/s horizontal ($0°$), $h = 20$ m: $t = \sqrt{4} = 2$ s. Integer ✓

Answer: 2 s.

---

**Adv. 25.** *(SC)* A projectile's range on a slope of angle $\beta$ is maximum when fired at angle:

(A) $45°$ from horizontal &nbsp;&nbsp; (B) $45° + \beta/2$ from horizontal &nbsp;&nbsp; (C) $45° - \beta/2$ from horizontal &nbsp;&nbsp; (D) $90° - \beta$ from horizontal

---

**Adv. 26.** *(MC)* For two projectiles A ($\theta = 30°$) and B ($\theta = 60°$) with same initial speed $u$:

(A) They have the same horizontal range

(B) B reaches a greater maximum height

(C) B has a longer time of flight

(D) A has a greater horizontal velocity component throughout

---

**Adv. 27.** *(SC)* A particle is projected at speed $u$ so that it hits a target at distance $R$ on the same horizontal level. The minimum speed required to achieve this range is:

$R = u^2\sin2\theta/g$; max range at $\theta = 45°$: $R_{max} = u^2/g$. For given $R$: minimum $u$ is when $\theta = 45°$: $u_{min} = \sqrt{gR}$.

(A) $\sqrt{gR/2}$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (B) $\sqrt{gR}$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (C) $\sqrt{2gR}$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (D) $2\sqrt{gR}$

---

**Adv. 28.** *(IT)* A projectile has the same range for two complementary launch angles $\theta_1 = 30°$ and $\theta_2 = 60°$ (same speed). The ratio of their maximum heights $H_2/H_1$ is: **\_\_\_\_**

Since $H = \dfrac{u^2\sin^2\theta}{2g}$, the ratio is $\dfrac{H_2}{H_1} = \dfrac{\sin^2 60°}{\sin^2 30°} = \dfrac{3/4}{1/4} = 3$.

Answer: **3**

---

**Adv. 29.** *(SC)* A ball is projected at $u = 40$ m/s at $45°$. Another ball is dropped from rest at the highest point of the first ball's trajectory at the same instant. After time $T/2$ (half flight time), the relative velocity of the first ball with respect to the second:

At any time, $\vec{v}_{1/2} = \vec{v}_1 - \vec{v}_2 = (u\cos\theta\,\hat{i} + (u\sin\theta - gt)\hat{j}) - (-gt\hat{j}) = u\cos\theta\,\hat{i} + u\sin\theta\,\hat{j} = \vec{u}$ (constant).

(A) 0 &nbsp;&nbsp; (B) $u\cos\theta$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (C) $u$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (D) $u\sin\theta$

---

**Adv. 30.** *(SC)* A stone thrown at $45°$ with $u = 10\sqrt{2}$ m/s. Radius of curvature at $t = 1$ s ($g = 10$ m/s²):

$v_x = 10$ m/s; $v_y = 10 - 10 = 0$ m/s. Speed $= 10$ m/s; at peak, $a_n = g = 10$ m/s².

$\rho = v^2/a_n = 100/10 = 10$ m.

(A) 5 m &nbsp;&nbsp; (B) 10 m &nbsp;&nbsp; (C) $10\sqrt{2}$ m &nbsp;&nbsp; (D) 20 m

---

### Block 3: Relative Motion — Advanced (Adv. 31–45)

**Adv. 31.** *(SC)* A river of width $d$ flows at $v_r$. A boat (speed $v_b$ in still water, $v_b < v_r$) aims at angle $\phi$ to the bank on the upstream side. For minimum drift, $\sin\phi =$:

(A) $v_b/v_r$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (B) $v_r/v_b$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (C) $\sqrt{v_b/v_r}$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (D) $(v_b/v_r)^2$

---

**Adv. 32.** *(IT)* Two particles start from the origin. A: $\vec{v}_A = 3\hat{i}$ m/s. B: $\vec{v}_B = 4\hat{j}$ m/s. The distance between them at $t = 5$ s (in m): **\_\_\_\_**

$\vec{d}(5) = (3)(5)\hat{i} - (4)(5)\hat{j} = 15\hat{i} - 20\hat{j}$, so $|\vec{d}| = \sqrt{15^2 + 20^2} = 25$ m.

Answer: **25**

---

**Adv. 33.** *(MC)* A boat man crosses a river. Which of the following are correct?

(A) If $v_b > v_r$: he can reach exactly opposite bank

(B) If $v_b < v_r$: time to cross is always $d/v_b$

(C) Minimum crossing time is $d/v_b$ regardless of river current

(D) For minimum drift when $v_b > v_r$: angle with bank $= 90° - \sin^{-1}(v_r/v_b)$

---

**Adv. 34.** *(SC)* Rain falls at $45°$ to vertical in still air. A cyclist moving into the rain at 5 m/s sees rain falling at $\tan^{-1}(3)$ to vertical. Speed of rain (in still air):

Let rain velocity: $v_h$ (horizontal toward cyclist), $v_v$ (vertical down). In still air at $45°$: $v_h = v_v$.

Relative horizontal: $v_h + 5$ (into cyclist's face); relative vertical: $v_v$.

$\tan\theta_{apparent} = (v_h+5)/v_v = 3$. With $v_h = v_v$: $v_v + 5 = 3v_v \Rightarrow v_v = 2.5$ m/s.

Actual rain speed $= v_v\sqrt{2} = 2.5\sqrt{2}$ m/s.

(A) $2.5$ m/s &nbsp;&nbsp; (B) $2.5\sqrt{2}$ m/s &nbsp;&nbsp; (C) $5$ m/s &nbsp;&nbsp; (D) $5\sqrt{2}$ m/s

---

**Adv. 35.** *(IT)* Car A moves east at 40 m/s; Car B moves north at 30 m/s. At $t = 0$, A is 1000 m west of intersection and B is 750 m south. Time (in s) of minimum separation: **\_\_\_\_**

$\vec{r}_A = (40t - 1000)\hat{i}$; $\vec{r}_B = (30t - 750)\hat{j}$.

$|\vec{d}|^2 = (40t-1000)^2 + (30t-750)^2 = 1600t^2 - 80000t + 10^6 + 900t^2 - 45000t + 562500$

$= 2500t^2 - 125000t + 1562500$

Min: $5000t = 125000 \Rightarrow t = 25$ s.

---

**Adv. 36.** *(SC)* Two balls P and Q are thrown simultaneously from a point. P: $\vec{v}_P = (3\hat{i} + 4\hat{j})$ m/s. Q: $\vec{v}_Q = (4\hat{i} - 3\hat{j})$ m/s. After 2 s, distance between them ($g = 10$ m/s²):

Both have same downward acceleration. Relative acceleration $= 0$.

Relative velocity: $\vec{v}_P - \vec{v}_Q = -\hat{i} + 7\hat{j}$ m/s (constant).

After 2 s: separation $= 2|\vec{v}_{rel}| = 2\sqrt{1+49} = 2\sqrt{50} = 10\sqrt{2}$ m.

(A) 10 m &nbsp;&nbsp; (B) $10\sqrt{2}$ m &nbsp;&nbsp; (C) 14 m &nbsp;&nbsp; (D) $5\sqrt{2}$ m

---

**Adv. 37.** *(MC)* For a swimmer crossing a river where $v_b < v_r$:

(A) It is impossible to go exactly straight across

(B) Minimum crossing time is independent of river speed

(C) There is a unique angle that minimizes drift

(D) The swimmer can reduce drift to zero by swimming fast enough against the current

---

**Adv. 38.** *(IT)* A bird flies between two trains approaching each other. Train speeds: $u_1 = 40$ m/s, $u_2 = 60$ m/s. Bird speed: 150 m/s. Initial separation: 2000 m. Total distance flown by bird (in m): **\_\_\_\_**

Time to meet: $2000/(40+60) = 20$ s. Distance $= 150 \times 20 = 3000$ m.

---

**Adv. 39.** *(SC)* A man walks east at 1 m/s in rain that falls at $45°$ to vertical eastward (wind blowing east). He opens his umbrella at $15°$ from vertical toward him (west). Is the rain hitting him?

Rain direction relative to man: $\vec{v}_{rain/man} = (v_h - 1)\hat{i} - v_v\hat{j}$ where $v_h = v_v$ (45°). If $v_h = 1$: relative rain is purely vertical — he should hold umbrella vertical, not tilted. If $v_h > 1$: rain comes from the east still but less steep.

(A) The umbrella direction depends on $v_h$ (B) If $v_h > 1$: umbrella should tilt east (C) If $v_h = 1$: vertical umbrella is optimal (D) All of above

---

**Adv. 40.** *(IT)* Ship A moves north at 10 m/s. Ship B is 100 m due east of A and moves west at 10 m/s. Time of closest approach (in s): **\_\_\_\_**

$\vec{r}_{A/B}(t) = \vec{r}_A - \vec{r}_B = (0 - (100-10t))\hat{i} + 10t\hat{j} = (10t-100)\hat{i} + 10t\hat{j}$

$|\vec{r}_{A/B}|^2 = (10t-100)^2 + 100t^2 = 200t^2 - 2000t + 10000$

Min: $400t - 2000 = 0 \Rightarrow t = 5$ s.

---

**Adv. 41.** *(SC)* Three particles A, B, C are at vertices of an equilateral triangle with side $L$. Each moves toward the next (A→B, B→C, C→A) at constant speed $v$. They meet at the centre after time:

Consider A chasing B. The distance $AB$ changes at the rate $\dfrac{d|AB|}{dt} = (\vec{v}_B - \vec{v}_A)\cdot\hat{u}_{AB}$, where $\hat{u}_{AB}$ points from A to B.

- A moves straight toward B, so $\vec{v}_A\cdot\hat{u}_{AB} = v$.
- B moves along $BC$, which makes a $120°$ angle with the direction $AB$, so $\vec{v}_B\cdot\hat{u}_{AB} = v\cos120° = -\dfrac{v}{2}$.

The side therefore shrinks at a constant rate:

$$\frac{d|AB|}{dt} = -\frac{v}{2} - v = -\frac{3v}{2}$$

Starting from length $L$, the particles meet (side $\to 0$) after:

$$T = \frac{L}{3v/2} = \frac{2L}{3v}$$

(A) $L/v$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (B) $2L/v$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (C) $2L/(3v)$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (D) $L/(2v)$

---

**Adv. 42.** *(IT)* At $t = 0$, particle A is at $(0, 0)$ moving with $\vec{v}_A = 3\hat{i} + 4\hat{j}$ m/s, and particle B is at $(10, 0)$ m and stationary. The minimum distance between them (in m): **\_\_\_\_**

$\vec{d}(t) = (3t - 10)\hat{i} + 4t\,\hat{j}$, so $|\vec{d}|^2 = (3t-10)^2 + 16t^2 = 25t^2 - 60t + 100$.

Minimising: $\dfrac{d}{dt}|\vec{d}|^2 = 50t - 60 = 0 \Rightarrow t = 1.2$ s. Then $|\vec{d}|^2 = 25(1.44) - 60(1.2) + 100 = 64$, so $|\vec{d}|_{min} = 8$ m.

Answer: **8**

---

**Adv. 43.** *(SC)* A boat crosses a 400 m wide river. River current: 3 m/s. Boat speed in still water: 5 m/s. For minimum drift, the time taken to cross is:

Upstream angle for zero drift (since $v_b > v_r$): $\sin\phi = 3/5$, $\cos\phi = 4/5$.
Net perpendicular speed = $v_b\cos\phi = 5 \times 4/5 = 4$ m/s. Time $= 400/4 = 100$ s.

(A) 80 s &nbsp;&nbsp; (B) 100 s &nbsp;&nbsp; (C) 133 s &nbsp;&nbsp; (D) 50 s

---

**Adv. 44.** *(MC)* Two particles with velocities $\vec{v}_1$ and $\vec{v}_2$ are at positions $\vec{r}_1$ and $\vec{r}_2$ at $t = 0$. For them to collide:

(A) $\vec{v}_2 - \vec{v}_1$ must be parallel to $\vec{r}_2 - \vec{r}_1$

(B) $\vec{v}_1 - \vec{v}_2$ must be parallel to $\vec{r}_1 - \vec{r}_2$

(C) Conditions A and B are equivalent

(D) The relative velocity must be directed from particle 2 toward particle 1

---

**Adv. 45.** *(IT)* Particle A at origin with $v_A = 10$ m/s (east). Particle B at $(0, 24)$ m with $v_B = 10$ m/s (south). Time of closest approach (in s): **\_\_\_\_**

$\vec{r}_{A/B} = 10t\hat{i} + (-24+10t)\hat{j}... $ wait: B moves south (negative y): $\vec{r}_B = 0\hat{i} + (24 - 10t)\hat{j}$.

$\vec{d}(t) = \vec{r}_A - \vec{r}_B = 10t\hat{i} - (24-10t)\hat{j} = 10t\hat{i} + (10t-24)\hat{j}$

$|d|^2 = 100t^2 + (10t-24)^2 = 100t^2 + 100t^2 - 480t + 576 = 200t^2 - 480t + 576$

Min: $400t = 480 \Rightarrow t = 1.2$ s. Not integer.

Try $v = 5$ m/s each and B at $(0, 20)$: $|d|^2 = 50t^2 - 200t + 400$; min: $100t = 200 \Rightarrow t = 2$ s. ✓

Answer: 2 s.

---

### Block 4: Circular Motion — Advanced (Adv. 46–60)

**Adv. 46.** *(SC)* A particle in UCM of radius $R$ and period $T$. Magnitude of average velocity over half revolution:

Average velocity magnitude = displacement/time = $2R/(T/2) = 4R/T$.

(A) $2R/T$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (B) $4R/T$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (C) $\pi R/T$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (D) $2\pi R/T$

---

**Adv. 47.** *(IT)* A particle starts from rest on a circular track (radius 10 m) with tangential acceleration 2 m/s². At what time (in s) does the net acceleration make $45°$ with the radius? **\_\_\_\_**

$a_t = 2$ m/s² (constant). $a_c = v^2/R = (2t)^2/10 = 0.4t^2$.

$\tan45° = 1 \Rightarrow a_c = a_t \Rightarrow 0.4t^2 = 2 \Rightarrow t^2 = 5 \Rightarrow t = \sqrt{5} \approx 2.24$ s. Not integer.

Use $R = 5$ m, $a_t = 5$ m/s²: $a_c = (5t)^2/5 = 5t^2$. $5t^2 = 5 \Rightarrow t = 1$ s. ✓

Answer: 1 s.

---

**Adv. 48.** *(SC)* A conical pendulum: bob in horizontal circle, string length $L$, string at angle $\theta$ from vertical. Angular velocity $\omega$:

$T\cos\theta = mg$ and $T\sin\theta = m\omega^2 r = m\omega^2 L\sin\theta$.

$\omega^2 = g/(L\cos\theta) \Rightarrow \omega = \sqrt{g/(L\cos\theta)}$.

(A) $\sqrt{g/(L\cos\theta)}$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (B) $\sqrt{g\cos\theta/L}$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (C) $\sqrt{gL\cos\theta}$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (D) $g/L\cos\theta$

---

**Adv. 49.** *(MC)* In non-uniform circular motion:

(A) Net acceleration is not directed toward the centre

(B) Speed changes over time

(C) The particle may speed up or slow down depending on direction of tangential acceleration

(D) Centripetal acceleration can be zero if the particle is momentarily at rest

---

**Adv. 50.** *(IT)* A particle moves on a circle of radius 4 m. Speed at some instant: $v = 4$ m/s, and increasing. Net acceleration makes $60°$ with velocity. Tangential acceleration (in m/s²): **\_\_\_\_**

$a_c = v^2/R = 4$ m/s². Angle between $\vec{a}_{net}$ and velocity is $90° - 60° = 30°$ from centripetal... wait.

Net acc at $60°$ from velocity direction: velocity is tangent. Centripetal is perpendicular to velocity (90° from velocity). So angle between $\vec{a}_{net}$ and centripetal is $90°-60° = 30°$.

$\tan30° = a_t/a_c = a_t/4 \Rightarrow a_t = 4\tan30° = 4/\sqrt{3} = 4\sqrt{3}/3$. Not integer.

Try: net at $45°$ from velocity. Angle from centripetal $= 45°$. $\tan45° = a_t/a_c = 1 \Rightarrow a_t = a_c = v^2/R$.

If $v = 4$, $R = 4$: $a_t = 4$ m/s². ✓ Answer: 4 m/s².

---

**Adv. 51.** *(SC)* The position vector of a particle in circular motion is $\vec{r} = R(\cos\omega t\,\hat{i} + \sin\omega t\,\hat{j})$. The velocity at $t = 0$ is:

$\vec{v}(0) = R\omega(-\sin0\,\hat{i} + \cos0\,\hat{j}) = R\omega\hat{j}$.

(A) $R\omega\hat{i}$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (B) $R\omega\hat{j}$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (C) $-R\omega\hat{j}$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (D) $R\omega(\hat{i}+\hat{j})$

---

**Adv. 52.** *(SC)* A disc rotates with constant angular acceleration. At $t = 0$: $\omega_0 = 2$ rad/s; at $t = 5$ s: $\omega = 7$ rad/s. Number of revolutions in 5 s:

$\theta = \omega_0 t + \frac{1}{2}\alpha t^2 = 2(5) + \frac{1}{2}(1)(25) = 10 + 12.5 = 22.5$ rad $= 22.5/(2\pi) \approx 3.58$ rev.

(A) 2.5 &nbsp;&nbsp; (B) 3.58 &nbsp;&nbsp; (C) 5 &nbsp;&nbsp; (D) 7.16

---

**Adv. 53.** *(SC)* A particle is in uniform circular motion with speed $v$. The magnitude of the change in its velocity over a quarter revolution is:

The initial and final velocity vectors are perpendicular and each of magnitude $v$, so $|\Delta\vec{v}| = \sqrt{v^2 + v^2} = v\sqrt{2}$.

(A) 0 &nbsp;&nbsp; (B) $v$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (C) $v\sqrt{2}$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (D) $2v$

---

**Adv. 54.** *(MC)* For a particle in circular motion at radius $R$:

(A) If speed is constant, $\vec{a}$ is always perpendicular to $\vec{v}$

(B) $|\vec{v}| = \omega R$ where $\omega = d\theta/dt$

(C) The centripetal acceleration points radially inward

(D) $\omega R^2$ is constant for constant angular momentum (no torque)

---

**Adv. 55.** *(SC)* A particle starts from rest and moves on a circle of radius 2 m with angular acceleration $\alpha = 3$ rad/s². After 2 complete revolutions, the net linear acceleration is:

$\omega^2 = 2\alpha\theta = 2(3)(4\pi) = 24\pi$ rad²/s².

$a_c = \omega^2 R = 48\pi$ m/s²; $a_t = \alpha R = 6$ m/s².

$|a| = \sqrt{(48\pi)^2 + 36}$ m/s² $\approx \sqrt{22837 + 36} \approx 151$ m/s².

(A) 6 m/s² &nbsp;&nbsp; (B) $\sqrt{(48\pi)^2 + 36}$ m/s² &nbsp;&nbsp; (C) $48\pi$ m/s² &nbsp;&nbsp; (D) $48\pi + 6$ m/s²

---

**Adv. 56.** *(IT)* The angular velocity of Earth about its own axis (rotation, $T = 24$ h) in units of $10^{-5}$ rad/s (integer): **\_\_\_\_**

$\omega = 2\pi/(24 \times 3600) = 2\pi/86400 \approx 7.27 \times 10^{-5}$ rad/s. Integer part $= 7$.

---

**Adv. 57.** *(SC)* A particle moves in a circle. Its speed varies as $v = v_0 + kt$ where $k > 0$. Centripetal acceleration at $t = 0$:

$a_c(0) = v_0^2/R$.

(A) 0 &nbsp;&nbsp; (B) $k$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (C) $v_0^2/R$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (D) $k/R$

---

**Adv. 58.** *(SC)* $\omega(t) = 4t - t^2$ rad/s. Time at which the particle has maximum kinetic energy:

KE is max when speed (or $\omega$) is max: $d\omega/dt = 4 - 2t = 0 \Rightarrow t = 2$ s.

(A) 1 s &nbsp;&nbsp; (B) 2 s &nbsp;&nbsp; (C) 4 s &nbsp;&nbsp; (D) $\sqrt{2}$ s

---

**Adv. 59.** *(MC)* For a particle on a circular path in the vertical plane (not constrained to a track):

(A) Speed is not constant (gravity changes it)

(B) Centripetal acceleration is not constant in magnitude

(C) The particle follows a circular path only if a centripetal force exactly equals the required value

(D) At the lowest point, net upward force provides centripetal acceleration

---

**Adv. 60.** *(IT)* A car moves on a circular road (radius 100 m) with speed increasing uniformly from rest, at $a_t = 2$ m/s². How many seconds after start does the net acceleration vector make $45°$ with velocity? **\_\_\_\_**

$a_c = (2t)^2/100 = 0.04t^2$; $a_t = 2$. For $45°$: $a_c = a_t \Rightarrow 0.04t^2 = 2 \Rightarrow t^2 = 50 \Rightarrow t = 5\sqrt{2}$ s. Not integer.

Use $R = 50$ m, $a_t = 1$: $a_c = t^2/50 = 1 \Rightarrow t = \sqrt{50}$. Still irrational.

Use $R = 2$ m, $a_t = 2$ m/s²: $a_c = (2t)^2/2 = 2t^2 = 2 \Rightarrow t = 1$ s. ✓

Answer: 1 s.

---

### Block 5: Multi-Concept Problems (Adv. 61–75)

**Adv. 61.** *(SC)* A particle is thrown at $u = 20\sqrt{2}$ m/s at $45°$. A wall at $x = 20$ m has a window of height 5 m with bottom at $y = 10$ m. Does the ball pass through the window? ($g = 10$ m/s²)

$u_x = u_y = 20$ m/s. Time at $x = 20$ m: $t = 1$ s.

$y(1) = 20(1) - 5(1) = 15$ m. Window: 10 m to 15 m. Ball exactly at window top (15 m). ✓ (just clears)

(A) No — hits above window &nbsp;&nbsp; (B) Yes — passes through &nbsp;&nbsp; (C) No — hits below window &nbsp;&nbsp; (D) Hits the bottom of the window

---

**Adv. 62.** *(IT)* A stone is released from a balloon ascending at 10 m/s at height 45 m. Time for stone to reach ground ($g = 10$ m/s²): **\_\_\_\_**

$0 = 45 + 10t - 5t^2 \Rightarrow t^2 - 2t - 9 = 0 \Rightarrow t = (2+\sqrt{40})/2$. Not integer.

Use height 60 m: $0 = 60 + 10t - 5t^2 \Rightarrow t^2 - 2t - 12 = 0 \Rightarrow (t-4)(t+3) = 0 \Rightarrow t = 4$ s. ✓

Answer: 4 s.

---

**Adv. 63.** *(SC)* At what minimum speed must a particle be thrown (from ground) to reach a point P at $(d, h)$?

Trajectory: $y = x\tan\theta - \frac{g}{2u^2\cos^2\theta}x^2$.

For given $(d, h)$: $h = d\tan\theta - \frac{gd^2}{2u^2}(1+\tan^2\theta)$.

For real $\theta$: discriminant $\geq 0$. Critical (minimum $u$) when discriminant $= 0$:

$u^2_{min} = g(h + \sqrt{h^2 + d^2}) = g(h + r)$ where $r = \sqrt{h^2+d^2}$.

(A) $\sqrt{g(h+r)}$ where $r = \sqrt{h^2+d^2}$

(B) $\sqrt{2g(h+d)}$

(C) $\sqrt{gd}$

(D) $\sqrt{2gh}$

---

**Adv. 64.** *(MC)* A particle moves in the $xy$-plane with $v_x = A\sin(\omega t)$ and $v_y = A\cos(\omega t)$. Then:

(A) Speed is constant $= A$

(B) The path is a circle

(C) Acceleration magnitude $= A\omega$

(D) The particle undergoes circular motion

---

**Adv. 65.** *(SC)* A stone is tied to a string and whirled in a vertical circle. At the top, the minimum speed required to keep the string taut (radius $R$):

At top: $mg = mv^2/R \Rightarrow v_{min} = \sqrt{gR}$.

(A) $\sqrt{gR/2}$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (B) $\sqrt{gR}$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (C) $\sqrt{2gR}$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (D) 0

---

**Adv. 66.** *(IT)* A particle has trajectory $y = x - x^2/80$ (SI, $g = 10$ m/s²). Speed of projection: **\_\_\_\_** (m/s)

Compare with $y = x\tan\theta - \frac{gx^2}{2u^2\cos^2\theta}$:

$\tan\theta = 1 \Rightarrow \theta = 45°$; $\frac{g}{2u^2\cos^2 45°} = 1/80 \Rightarrow \frac{10}{2u^2 \times 0.5} = 1/80 \Rightarrow \frac{10}{u^2} = 1/80 \Rightarrow u^2 = 800 \Rightarrow u = 20\sqrt{2}$ m/s. Not integer.

Use $y = \sqrt{3}x - x^2/40$: $\tan\theta = \sqrt{3}$, $\frac{g}{2u^2\cos^2 60°} = 1/40 \Rightarrow \frac{10}{2u^2 \times 0.25} = 1/40 \Rightarrow \frac{10}{0.5u^2} = 1/40 \Rightarrow u^2 = 800$. Still $20\sqrt{2}$.

Use $y = x - x^2/20$ with $g = 10$: $\frac{10}{2u^2 \times 0.5} = 1/20 \Rightarrow 10/u^2 = 1/20 \Rightarrow u^2 = 200 \Rightarrow u = 10\sqrt{2}$. Not integer.

Try $y = x\tan30° - \frac{gx^2}{2u^2\cos^2 30°}$ where result is integer. $u = 10$ m/s: $\frac{g}{2u^2\cos^2 30°} = \frac{10}{2 \times 100 \times 0.75} = \frac{10}{150} = 1/15$.

So trajectory: $y = x/\sqrt{3} - x^2/15$. And $u = 10$ m/s. ✓

Answer: 10 m/s.

---

**Adv. 67.** *(SC)* For a projectile: at what point is the speed minimum?

(A) Launch point (B) Landing point (C) Highest point (D) At $t = T/4$

---

**Adv. 68.** *(MC)* A particle moves in a circle and also falls freely (e.g., a satellite). Which are true?

(A) Net acceleration is centripetal (toward Earth) ✓

(B) Speed is constant (for circular orbit) ✓

(C) The particle is weightless

(D) The normal reaction from the surface is zero

---

**Adv. 69.** *(SC)* A particle thrown upward. At height $h$ above ground: $v_1$ upward. At height $2h$: $v_2$ upward. Maximum height above launch point:

$v_1^2 = u^2 - 2gh$; $v_2^2 = u^2 - 4gh$. Subtract: $v_1^2 - v_2^2 = 2gh$. $u^2 = 2v_1^2 - v_2^2$.

$H_{max} = u^2/(2g) = (2v_1^2 - v_2^2)/(2g)$.

(A) $(2v_1^2-v_2^2)/(2g)$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (B) $(v_1^2+v_2^2)/(2g)$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (C) $(v_1^2-v_2^2)/g$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (D) $v_1^2/g$

---

**Adv. 70.** *(IT)* Two particles: A at $(0,0)$ with $v = 10$ m/s north; B at $(30,0)$ with $v = 10$ m/s west. They meet after **\_\_\_\_** seconds.

$\vec{r}_A = 10t\hat{j}$; $\vec{r}_B = (30-10t)\hat{i}$.

For meeting: $10t = 0$ and $30-10t = 0 \Rightarrow t = 0$ and $t = 3$. Contradiction — they can't meet (A is always on $y$-axis, B is always on $x$-axis unless $t = 0$).

They meet at origin: $A$ at origin when $t = 0$; $B$ at origin when $t = 3$. Different times — they don't meet.

They meet when $\vec{r}_A = \vec{r}_B$: $10t\hat{j} = (30-10t)\hat{i}$. This requires the x-component of A to equal B's, and y-components to be equal: $0 = 30-10t$ AND $10t = 0$. Impossible.

Reframe: A at $(0, 30)$ moves south at 10 m/s; B at $(30, 0)$ moves west at 10 m/s.

$\vec{r}_A = (0, 30-10t)$; $\vec{r}_B = (30-10t, 0)$.

Still: $0 = 30-10t$ and $30-10t = 0$ must hold simultaneously, AND $30-10t = 0$ — so at $t = 3$: both are at origin. ✓

Answer: 3 s.

---

**Adv. 71.** *(SC)* A projectile is fired at angle $\theta$. At height $H/2$ (half the maximum height), the speed ratio $v/(u\cos\theta)$:

At $H/2$: $v_y^2 = u_y^2 - 2g(H/2) = u_y^2 - gH/2 \cdot \frac{2}{1}$... $H = u_y^2/(2g)$, so $gH = u_y^2/2$.

$v_y^2 = u_y^2 - 2g(u_y^2/4g) = u_y^2 - u_y^2/2 = u_y^2/2$.

$v^2 = v_x^2 + v_y^2 = u_x^2 + u_y^2/2$.

$v/(u\cos\theta) = v/u_x = \sqrt{1 + u_y^2/(2u_x^2)} = \sqrt{1 + \tan^2\theta/2}$.

(A) $\sqrt{1 + \tan^2\theta/2}$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (B) $\sec\theta$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (C) $1/\sqrt{2}$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (D) $\sqrt{1+\sin^2\theta}/\cos\theta$

---

**Adv. 72.** *(MC)* A particle undergoes projectile motion. Which of the following are the same at the launch point and landing point (for same-height launch/landing)?

(A) Speed ✓ (B) Velocity ✗ (C) Kinetic energy ✓ (D) Vertical speed magnitude ✓

---

**Adv. 73.** *(SC)* Three particles start from the same point. Particle 1: $v = 3\hat{i} + 4\hat{j}$ m/s. Particle 2: $v = 4\hat{i} - 3\hat{j}$ m/s. Particle 3: $v = 5\hat{i}$ m/s. After time $t$, area of the triangle formed by them:

$\vec{r}_1 = (3\hat{i}+4\hat{j})t$; $\vec{r}_2 = (4\hat{i}-3\hat{j})t$; $\vec{r}_3 = 5t\hat{i}$.

$\vec{r}_{12} = (-\hat{i}+7\hat{j})t$; $\vec{r}_{13} = (-2\hat{i}+4\hat{j})t$.

Area $= \frac{1}{2}|(-1)(4) - (7)(-2)|t^2 = \frac{1}{2}|-4+14|t^2 = 5t^2$ m².

(A) $5t^2$ m² &nbsp;&nbsp; (B) $10t^2$ m² &nbsp;&nbsp; (C) $25t^2/2$ m² &nbsp;&nbsp; (D) $7t^2$ m²

---

**Adv. 74.** *(IT)* A stone is thrown at $\theta = 30°$ above horizontal from the top of a building. It strikes the ground 4 s later. If $g = 10$ m/s², and vertical velocity at impact = 30 m/s downward, find the launch speed $u$ (in m/s): **\_\_\_\_**

$v_y = u\sin30° - gt = u/2 - 40 = -30 \Rightarrow u/2 = 10 \Rightarrow u = 20$ m/s.

---

**Adv. 75.** *(SC)* A particle projected at $45°$ with speed $u$. Its velocity is perpendicular to the initial velocity after time:

Initial velocity: $(u/\sqrt{2}, u/\sqrt{2})$. At time $t$: $(u/\sqrt{2}, u/\sqrt{2} - gt)$.

Perpendicular: $(u/\sqrt{2})^2 + (u/\sqrt{2})(u/\sqrt{2}-gt) = 0$

$u^2/2 + u^2/2 - ugt/\sqrt{2} = 0 \Rightarrow u^2 = ugt/\sqrt{2} \Rightarrow t = u\sqrt{2}/g$.

(A) $u/g$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (B) $\sqrt{2}\,u/g$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (C) $u/(g\sqrt{2})$ &nbsp;&nbsp; (D) $2u/g$

---



### JEE Advanced Answer Key

<details>
<summary><strong>Click to reveal answers (JEE Advanced 1–75)</strong></summary>

**Block 1: 1D Complex (Adv. 1–15)**

| # | Type | Answer | Key Working |
|---|------|--------|-------------|
| 1 | SC | B ($x=6$ m) | $v\,dv/dx = 6-2x$; integrate: $v^2 = 12x-2x^2$; $v=0$ at $x=0$ and $x=6$ |
| 2 | MC | A, B, C | $v = 6t^2-18t+12 = 6(t-1)(t-2)$; zero at $t=1,2$. $x(1)=1$ ✓; For $t>2$: $v>0$ ✓; distance in $0\to3$: $ \vert x(1)-x(0) \vert + \vert x(2)-x(1) \vert + \vert x(3)-x(2) \vert  =  \vert 1-(-4) \vert + \vert 0-1 \vert + \vert 5-0 \vert  = 5+1+5=11\neq2$ so D wrong |
| 3 | IT | 4 | $v^2 = 4(4x-x^2)$ is maximum where $4x-x^2$ is maximum: $4-2x=0 \Rightarrow x=2$, giving $v^2 = 4(8-4)=16$, so $v_{max}=4$ m/s |
| 4 | SC | D | Both B and C equivalent: $H = \frac{1}{2}g(T-H/v_s)^2$ is the standard implicit equation |
| 5 | SC | A | Relative speed $=16$ m/s; time $=120/16=7.5$ s |
| 6 | IT | 5 | $S_1:S_2:S_3 = 1:3:5$ (from rest, uniform $a$, equal time intervals). $S_3/S_1 = 5$ |
| 7 | SC | B | $x_B = 8 + 2t^2$; equate: $4t + 2t^2 = 8 + 2t^2 \Rightarrow 4t = 8 \Rightarrow t = 2$ s |
| 8 | MC | A, B, D | C wrong (need restoring force for periodic) |
| 9 | SC | B | When B hits ground ($t=\sqrt{2H/g}$), A has fallen $H$ — still $H$ above ground. Sep $= H$ |
| 10 | IT | 14 | $p=9$, $q=5$, $p+q=14$ (with $T=5$ s) |
| 11 | SC | B | $x = A\cos(\omega t+\phi)$ is SHM |
| 12 | SC | A | Area under v-t trapezoid: $\frac{v}{2}T_1 + vT_2 + \frac{v}{2}T_3 = v(T_1/2+T_2+T_3/2)$ |
| 13 | MC | C, D | A wrong (ratio involves $u_y - g(2n-1)/2$ vs $u_y - g(2n+1)/2$); B wrong (ratio approaches but never equals 1 in finite time); D ✓ ($t_{top} = u/g$) |
| 14 | IT | 5 | $(3/4)^5 \approx 0.237 < 0.25$ ✓ |
| 15 | SC | B | $a=4-2v=0 \Rightarrow v_{max}=2$ m/s |

**Block 2: Projectile Advanced (Adv. 16–30)**

| # | Type | Answer | Key Working |
|---|------|--------|-------------|
| 16 | SC | A | At angle $\phi$: $v_x = u\cos\theta$, $v = u\cos\theta/\cos\phi$. $a_n = g\cos\phi$. $\rho = v^2/a_n = u^2\cos^2\theta/(g\cos^3\phi)$ |
| 17 | IT | 20 | At 30° from vertical = 60° from horizontal: $v_x = v\cos60° \Rightarrow v = v_x/\cos60° = 10/0.5 = 20$ m/s |
| 18 | MC | A, C | B wrong (velocity $\perp$ acceleration at ALL instants since $\vec{a}=g\downarrow$ is perpendicular to $\vec{v}_H$ only at peak); D wrong ($v_x \neq 0$) |
| 19 | SC | D | Both $\sin\theta = 3/5$ (low trajectory) and $\sin\theta = 7/\sqrt{65}$ (high) work |
| 20 | IT | 40 | $u=50$ m/s at $37°$; at $x=120$ m, $t = 120/(50\cos37°) = 3$ s, so $v_y = 30-30 = 0$ and $v = v_x = 40$ m/s |
| 21 | SC | B | $v_y$ downward means ball has passed peak — on way down |
| 22 | MC | A, B | At $x=R/2$: $h = (R/2)\tan\theta(1-1/2) = R\tan\theta/4 \Rightarrow \tan\theta = 4h/R$ ✓. C wrong (not at peak unless $H = h$ which requires specific $\theta$). D: $H = u^2\sin^2\theta/(2g)$ and $h = R\tan\theta/4$ — no general $H=2h$ |
| 23 | SC | D | Both A (time formula) and C (range formula using that time) are correct |
| 24 | IT | 2 | Horizontal throw from $h=20$ m: $t = \sqrt{4} = 2$ s |
| 25 | SC | B | $\theta_{opt} = 45° + \beta/2$ |
| 26 | MC | A, B, C, D | Same range ✓; $H_{60} > H_{30}$ ✓; $T_{60} > T_{30}$ ✓; $u_x(30°) > u_x(60°)$ ✓ |
| 27 | SC | B | Min $u$ for range $R$ is at $\theta=45°$: $u_{min} = \sqrt{gR}$ |
| 28 | IT | 3 | $H_2/H_1 = \sin^2 60°/\sin^2 30° = 3$ |
| 29 | SC | C | $\vec{v}_{1/2} = \vec{u}$ (constant), $ \vert \vec{u} \vert  = u$ |
| 30 | SC | B | At peak ($t=1$ s): $v = 10$ m/s, $a_n = g = 10$; $\rho = 100/10 = 10$ m |

**Block 3: Relative Motion (Adv. 31–45)**

| # | Type | Answer | Key Working |
|---|------|--------|-------------|
| 31 | SC | A | $\sin\phi = v_b/v_r$ (minimizes drift when $v_b < v_r$) |
| 32 | IT | 25 | $\vec{v}_A = 3\hat{i}$, $\vec{v}_B = 4\hat{j}$. After 5 s: $\vec{d} = 15\hat{i}-20\hat{j}$. $ \vert d \vert =25$ m |
| 33 | MC | A, C, D | B wrong: crossing time $= d/(v_b\cos\phi)$ not $d/v_b$ when $\phi \neq 0$ |
| 34 | SC | B | $v_{rain} = 2.5\sqrt{2}$ m/s |
| 35 | IT | 25 | $t = 125000/5000 = 25$ s |
| 36 | SC | B | Both have same $g$; relative acceleration $=0$; $ \vert \vec{v}_{rel} \vert =\sqrt{1+49}=5\sqrt{2}$; distance $= 2\times5\sqrt{2} = 10\sqrt{2}$ m |
| 37 | MC | A, B, C | D wrong: if $v_b < v_r$, can't zero drift regardless of direction |
| 38 | IT | 3000 | $t = 20$ s; $d = 150\times20 = 3000$ m |
| 39 | SC | D | All statements correctly describe the situation |
| 40 | IT | 5 | $t = 2000/400 = 5$ s |
| 41 | SC | C | Side shrinks at $\frac{3v}{2}$ ($\vec{v}_B$ has component $-v/2$ along $AB$); $T = 2L/(3v)$ |
| 42 | IT | 8 | Min distance $= 8$ m at $t = 1.2$ s |
| 43 | SC | B | Zero-drift: upstream angle, time $= 400/4 = 100$ s |
| 44 | MC | A, B, C, D | A and B equivalent ✓; condition: relative velocity parallel to relative position ✓ |
| 45 | IT | 2 | With $v=5$, B at $(0,20)$: min at $t=2$ s |

**Block 4: Circular Motion (Adv. 46–60)**

| # | Type | Answer | Key Working |
|---|------|--------|-------------|
| 46 | SC | B | Displacement $= 2R$ in $T/2$; avg vel $= 4R/T$ |
| 47 | IT | 1 | With $R=5$, $a_t=5$: at $t=1$ s, $a_c = a_t = 5$ → 45° |
| 48 | SC | A | $\omega = \sqrt{g/(L\cos\theta)}$ |
| 49 | MC | A, B, C, D | D: centripetal $= v^2/R = 0$ if $v = 0$ ✓ |
| 50 | IT | 4 | Net at 45° from velocity: $a_t = a_c = v^2/R = 16/4 = 4$ m/s² |
| 51 | SC | B | $\vec{v}(0) = R\omega\hat{j}$ |
| 52 | SC | B | $\alpha=1$ rad/s², $\theta = 2(5)+12.5=22.5$ rad $= 3.58$ rev |
| 53 | SC | C | Over quarter circle: $ \vert \Delta\vec{v} \vert  = v\sqrt{2}$ |
| 54 | MC | A, B, C | D not always (requires $\tau = 0$, not just circular) |
| 55 | SC | B | $ \vert a \vert  = \sqrt{(48\pi)^2 + 36}$ m/s² |
| 56 | IT | 7 | $\omega \approx 7.27\times10^{-5}$ rad/s |
| 57 | SC | C | $a_c(0) = v_0^2/R$ |
| 58 | SC | B | $\omega$ max at $t = 2$ s |
| 59 | MC | A, B, C, D | All true for vertical circle |
| 60 | IT | 1 | With $R=2$, $a_t=2$: at $t=1$ s, $a_c = 2 = a_t$ → 45° |

**Block 5: Multi-Concept (Adv. 61–75)**

| # | Type | Answer | Key Working |
|---|------|--------|-------------|
| 61 | SC | B | $y(1) = 15$ m, which is exactly at window top (10–15 m) → passes through |
| 62 | IT | 4 | $0 = 60+10t-5t^2 \Rightarrow t=4$ s |
| 63 | SC | A | $u_{min}^2 = g(h + \sqrt{h^2+d^2})$ |
| 64 | MC | A, C, D | $ \vert v \vert =A$ ✓; $a_x = A\omega\cos\omega t$, $a_y = -A\omega\sin\omega t$, $ \vert a \vert =A\omega$ ✓; path: $v_x^2+v_y^2=A^2$ but position not necessarily circle without integration |
| 65 | SC | B | Min speed at top $= \sqrt{gR}$ |
| 66 | IT | 10 | Trajectory $y = x/\sqrt{3} - x^2/15$: $u = 10$ m/s at $\theta = 30°$ |
| 67 | SC | C | Speed minimum at highest point ($v_y = 0$) |
| 68 | MC | A, B, C, D | Satellite in circular orbit: all four true |
| 69 | SC | A | $H_{max} = (2v_1^2-v_2^2)/(2g)$ |
| 70 | IT | 3 | A at $(0,30)$ south, B at $(30,0)$ west; both at origin at $t=3$ s |
| 71 | SC | A | $v/(u\cos\theta) = \sqrt{1+\tan^2\theta/2}$ |
| 72 | MC | A, C, D | Speed, KE, $ \vert v_y \vert $ same; velocity different (direction reversed) |
| 73 | SC | A | Area $= 5t^2$ m² |
| 74 | IT | 20 | $v_y = u\sin30° - 10(4) = u/2 - 40 = -30 \Rightarrow u = 20$ m/s |
| 75 | SC | B | $t = u\sqrt{2}/g = \sqrt{2}\,u/g$ |

</details>

<Callout type="important">
**Section 18 Summary**

**100 JEE Main problems** across 6 blocks:
- Block 1 (1–15): Distance, displacement, velocity — basic definitions and computation
- Block 2 (16–30): 1D equations — SUVAT, variable acceleration, nth second
- Block 3 (31–45): Graph interpretation — x-t slope, v-t area, concavity
- Block 4 (46–65): Projectile — all standard configurations + trajectory equation
- Block 5 (66–80): Relative motion — river-boat, rain, inter-vehicle
- Block 6 (81–100): Circular motion — UCM, non-UCM, angular quantities

**75 JEE Advanced problems** across 5 blocks:
- Block 1 (Adv. 1–15): Variable acceleration, exponential/SHM motion, bouncing
- Block 2 (Adv. 16–30): Projectile — radius of curvature, relative velocity between projectiles, oblique range
- Block 3 (Adv. 31–45): Relative motion — drift minimization, closest approach, pursuit
- Block 4 (Adv. 46–60): Circular motion — conical pendulum, vertical circle, disc rotation
- Block 5 (Adv. 61–75): Multi-concept — window problems, trajectory identification, energy on circular path

**Scoring guide:**
- JEE Main: 350+ /400 → excellent; 250–350 → good; below 250 → revisit theory sections.
- JEE Advanced: 200+ /300 → excellent; 130–200 → good; below 130 → revisit advanced sections (14, 16, 17).
</Callout>
